699:     describe("cloneRepository with sourceBranch", () => {
700:       it("should clone Git repository without sourceBranch (existing behavior)", async () => {
701:         const vcs = new VCS();
702:         const { execSync } = await import("child_process");
703:         const sourcePath = join(testHome, "source-repo");
704:         
705:         // Create a source repo
706:         mkdirSync(sourcePath, { recursive: true });
707:         execSync("git init", { cwd: sourcePath });
708:         execSync("git config user.email \"test@test.com\"", { cwd: sourcePath });
709:         execSync("git config user.name \"Test User\"", { cwd: sourcePath });
710:         
711:         const { writeFileSync } = await import("fs");
712:         writeFileSync(join(sourcePath, "README.md"), "# Source Repo");
713:         execSync("git add .", { cwd: sourcePath });
714:         execSync('git commit -m "Initial commit"', { cwd: sourcePath });
715:         
716:       execSync("git checkout -b feature/v2", { cwd: sourcePath });
717:       writeFileSync(join(sourcePath, "feature.txt"), "feature content");
718:       execSync("git add .", { cwd: sourcePath });
719:       execSync('git commit -m "Feature commit"', { cwd: sourcePath });
720:       
721:       // Switch back to master
722:       execSync("git checkout master", { cwd: sourcePath });
723:         
724:         // Clone without sourceBranch - should clone default branch (main)
725:         const targetPath = join(testHome, "cloned-repo-default");
726:         const result = await vcs.cloneRepository(sourcePath, "git", targetPath);
727:         
728:         expect(result.success).toBe(true);
729:         expect(existsSync(join(targetPath, "README.md"))).toBe(true);
730:         expect(existsSync(join(targetPath, "feature.txt"))).toBe(false);
731:       }, 15000);
732: 
733:       it("should clone Git repository with sourceBranch", async () => {
734:         const vcs = new VCS();
735:         const { execSync } = await import("child_process");
736:         const sourcePath = join(testHome, "source-repo-branch");
737:         
738:         // Create a source repo
739:         mkdirSync(sourcePath, { recursive: true });
740:         execSync("git init", { cwd: sourcePath });
741:         execSync("git config user.email \"test@test.com\"", { cwd: sourcePath });
742:         execSync("git config user.name \"Test User\"", { cwd: sourcePath });
743:         
744:         const { writeFileSync } = await import("fs");
745:         writeFileSync(join(sourcePath, "main.txt"), "main content");
746:         execSync("git add .", { cwd: sourcePath });
747:         execSync('git commit -m "Main commit"', { cwd: sourcePath });
748:         
749:       execSync("git checkout -b feature/v2", { cwd: sourcePath });
750:       writeFileSync(join(sourcePath, "feature.txt"), "feature content");
751:       execSync("git add .", { cwd: sourcePath });
752:       execSync('git commit -m "Feature commit"', { cwd: sourcePath });
753:       
754:       // Switch back to master
755:       execSync("git checkout master", { cwd: sourcePath });
756:

````
<skill_content name="openspec-verify-change">
# Skill: openspec-verify-change

Verify that an implementation matches the change artifacts (specs, tasks, design).

**Input**: Optionally specify a change name. If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.

**Steps**

1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**

   Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.

   Show changes that have implementation tasks (tasks artifact exists).
   Include the schema used for each change if available.
   Mark changes with incomplete tasks as "(In Progress)".

   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.

2. **Check status to understand the schema**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to understand:
   - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
   - Which artifacts exist for this change

3. **Get the change directory and load artifacts**

   ```bash
   openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
   ```

   This returns the change directory and context files. Read all available artifacts from `contextFiles`.

4. **Initialize verification report structure**

   Create a report structure with three dimensions:
   - **Completeness**: Track tasks and spec coverage
   - **Correctness**: Track requirement implementation and scenario coverage
   - **Coherence**: Track design adherence and pattern consistency

   Each dimension can have CRITICAL, WARNING, or SUGGESTION issues.

5. **Verify Completeness**

   **Task Completion**:
   - If tasks.md exists in contextFiles, read it
   - Parse checkboxes: `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete)
   - Count complete vs total tasks
   - If incomplete tasks exist:
     - Add CRITICAL issue for each incomplete task
     - Recommendation: "Complete task: <description>" or "Mark as done if already implemented"

   **Spec Coverage**:
   - If delta specs exist in `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`:
     - Extract all requirements (marked with "### Requirement:")
     - For each requirement:
       - Search codebase for keywords related to the requirement
       - Assess if implementation likely exists
     - If requirements appear unimplemented:
       - Add CRITICAL issue: "Requirement not found: <requirement name>"
       - Recommendation: "Implement requirement X: <description>"

6. **Verify Correctness**

   **Requirement Implementation Mapping**:
   - For each requirement from delta specs:
     - Search codebase for implementation evidence
     - If found, note file paths and line ranges
     - Assess if implementation matches requirement intent
     - If divergence detected:
       - Add WARNING: "Implementation may diverge from spec: <details>"
       - Recommendation: "Review <file>:<lines> against requirement X"

   **Scenario Coverage**:
   - For each scenario in delta specs (marked with "#### Scenario:"):
     - Check if conditions are handled in code
     - Check if tests exist covering the scenario
     - If scenario appears uncovered:
       - Add WARNING: "Scenario not covered: <scenario name>"
       - Recommendation: "Add test or implementation for scenario: <description>"

7. **Verify Coherence**

   **Design Adherence**:
   - If design.md exists in contextFiles:
     - Extract key decisions (look for sections like "Decision:", "Approach:", "Architecture:")
     - Verify implementation follows those decisions
     - If contradiction detected:
       - Add WARNING: "Design decision not followed: <decision>"
       - Recommendation: "Update implementation or revise design.md to match reality"
   - If no design.md: Skip design adherence check, note "No design.md to verify against"

   **Code Pattern Consistency**:
   - Review new code for consistency with project patterns
   - Check file naming, directory structure, coding style
   - If significant deviations found:
     - Add SUGGESTION: "Code pattern deviation: <details>"
     - Recommendation: "Consider following project pattern: <example>"

8. **Generate Verification Report**

   **Summary Scorecard**:
   ```
   ## Verification Report: <change-name>

   ### Summary
   | Dimension    | Status           |
   |--------------|------------------|
   | Completeness | X/Y tasks, N reqs|
   | Correctness  | M/N reqs covered |
   | Coherence    | Followed/Issues  |
   ```

   **Issues by Priority**:

   1. **CRITICAL** (Must fix before archive):
      - Incomplete tasks
      - Missing requirement implementations
      - Each with specific, actionable recommendation

   2. **WARNING** (Should fix):
      - Spec/design divergences
      - Missing scenario coverage
      - Each with specific recommendation

   3. **SUGGESTION** (Nice to fix):
      - Pattern inconsistencies
      - Minor improvements
      - Each with specific recommendation

   **Final Assessment**:
   - If CRITICAL issues: "X critical issue(s) found. Fix before archiving."
   - If only warnings: "No critical issues. Y warning(s) to consider. Ready for archive (with noted improvements)."
   - If all clear: "All checks passed. Ready for archive."

**Verification Heuristics**

- **Completeness**: Focus on objective checklist items (checkboxes, requirements list)
- **Correctness**: Use keyword search, file path analysis, reasonable inference - don't require perfect certainty
- **Coherence**: Look for glaring inconsistencies, don't nitpick style
- **False Positives**: When uncertain, prefer SUGGESTION over WARNING, WARNING over CRITICAL
- **Actionability**: Every issue must have a specific recommendation with file/line references where applicable

**Graceful Degradation**

- If only tasks.md exists: verify task completion only, skip spec/design checks
- If tasks + specs exist: verify completeness and correctness, skip design
- If full artifacts: verify all three dimensions
- Always note which checks were skipped and why

**Output Format**

Use clear markdown with:
- Table for summary scorecard
- Grouped lists for issues (CRITICAL/WARNING/SUGGESTION)
- Code references in format: `file.ts:123`
- Specific, actionable recommendations
- No vague suggestions like "consider reviewing"

Base directory for this skill: file:///home/bit4bit/src/mimo/.opencode/skills/openspec-verify-change
Relative paths in this skill (e.g., scripts/, reference/) are relative to this base directory.
Note: file list is sampled.

<skill_files>

</skill_files>
</skill_content>
````

30:     // Step 0: Get session and project
31:     const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
32:     if (!session) {
33:       return {
34:         success: false,
35:         message: "Session not found",
36:         error: "Session not found",
37:         step: null,
38:       };
39:     }
40: 
41:     const project = await projectRepository.findById(session.projectId);
42:     if (!project) {
43:       return {

47:         step: null,

56:     const { join } = await import("path");
57:     const fslckoutPath = join(session.agentWorkspacePath, ".fslckout");
58:

61:       const openResult = await vcs.openFossil(fossilPath, session.agentWorkspacePath);
62:       if (!openResult.success) {
63:         console.error(`[commit] Failed to initialize checkout: ${openResult.error}`);
64:         return {

67:           error: openResult.error || "Checkout initialization failed",
68:           step: null,
69:         };
70:       }
71:     }
72:

75:     const syncResult = await vcs.fossilUp(session.agentWorkspacePath);
76:     if (!syncResult.success) {
77:       // Check if it's because checkout doesn't exist
78:       if (syncResult.error?.includes("not within an open check-out") ||
79:           syncResult.error?.includes("current directory is not within")) {
80:         console.log(`[commit] Checkout not initialized, opening fossil repo...`);
81:         const openResult = await vcs.openFossil(fossilPath, session.agentWorkspacePath);
82:         if (!openResult.success) {
83:           return {
84:             success: false,
85:             message: "Failed to open fossil checkout",
86:             error: openResult.error || "fossil open failed",
87:             step: "sync",
88:           };
89:         }
90:         // Retry fossil up after opening
91:         const retryResult = await vcs.fossilUp(session.agentWorkspacePath);
92:         if (!retryResult.success) {
93:           return {
94:             success: false,
95:             message: "Failed to sync with agent",
96:             error: retryResult.error || "fossil up failed after open",

98:           };
99:         }
100:       } else {

106:         };

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-07 00:40:21)

I can see the issue now. Looking at the commit service in `service.ts`:

1. Line 158: `const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);`

This calls `pushUpstream` WITHOUT the `branch` parameter. Let me check the `pushUpstream` method in the VCS layer to confirm.

Looking at the `vcs/index.ts` file I read earlier:
- Lines 670-743: `pushToRemote` method (which seems to be the same as `pushUpstream`?)
- Lines 953-1023: `pushUpstream` method

Looking at line 158 of `service.ts`, it calls:
```typescript
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```

This only passes 2 arguments, but the method signature is:
```typescript
async pushUpstream(
  upstreamPath: string,
  repoType: "git" | "fossil",
  credential?: Credential,
  branch?: string
): Promise<VCSResult>
```

So it's missing the `branch` parameter! When `branch` is undefined, looking at lines 972:
```typescript
const pushArgs = branch ? ["push", "origin", branch] : ["push", "origin"];
```

So it only does `git push origin` without the branch name. This means the new branch won't be pushed to remote.

The fix is to pass `project.newBranch` to the `pushUpstream` call in `commitService.commitAndPush()`.

Let me verify this is the issue and create a fix.
## Agent (2026-04-07 00:40:26)

I found the issue! The commit service is not passing the `newBranch` when pushing to remote. Let me verify and fix this.

    it("should push to newBranch when project has newBranch configured", async () => {
      const vcs = new VCS();
      const sessionRepo = new SessionRepository();
      const projectRepo = new ProjectRepository();

      // Create a remote repo
      const remotePath = join(testHome, "remote-repo");
      mkdirSync(remotePath, { recursive: true });
      execSync("git init --bare", { cwd: remotePath });

      // Create a project with newBranch
      const project = await projectRepo.create({
        name: "Test Project",
        repoUrl: remotePath,
        repoType: "git",
        owner: "testuser",
        newBranch: "ai-session-feature-x",
      });

      // Create a session
      const session = await sessionRepo.create({
        name: "Test Session",
        projectId: project.id,
        owner: "testuser",
      });

      // Initialize upstream as Git repo with remote
      const upstreamPath = session.upstreamPath;
      mkdirSync(upstreamPath, { recursive: true });
      execSync("git init", { cwd: upstreamPath });
      execSync("git config user.email \"test@test.com\"", { cwd: upstreamPath });
      execSync("git config user.name \"Test User\"", { cwd: upstreamPath });
      execSync(`git remote add origin ${remotePath}`, { cwd: upstreamPath });
      
      // Create initial commit and push to master
      writeFileSync(join(upstreamPath, "initial.txt"), "initial");
      execSync("git add .", { cwd: upstreamPath });
      execSync('git commit -m "Initial commit"', { cwd: upstreamPath });
      execSync("git push origin master", { cwd: upstreamPath });

      // Create the new branch in upstream
      await vcs.createBranch("ai-session-feature-x", "git", upstreamPath);

      // Initialize agent-workspace with fossil
      const agentWorkspacePath = session.agentWorkspacePath;
      const fossilPath = join(testHome, "repo.fossil");
      await vcs.createFossilRepo(fossilPath);
      mkdirSync(agentWorkspacePath, { recursive: true });
      await vcs.openFossil(fossilPath, agentWorkspacePath);

      // Add a file to agent workspace
      writeFileSync(join(agentWorkspacePath, "test.txt"), "test content");

      // Commit in agent workspace
      await vcs.execCommand(["fossil", "add", "."], agentWorkspacePath);
      await vcs.execCommand(["fossil", "commit", "-m", "Agent commit"], agentWorkspacePath);

      // Run commit and push
      const result = await CommitService.commitAndPush(session.id);

      expect(result.success).toBe(true);
      expect(result.message).toContain("committed and pushed");

      // Verify the branch was pushed to remote
      const remoteBranches = execSync("git branch -a", { cwd: remotePath, encoding: "utf8" });
      expect(remoteBranches).toContain("ai-session-feature-x");
    }, 30000);

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-07 00:41:41)

The 2 failing tests are unrelated to my changes - they're about fossil server lifecycle. The tests I care about (projects and VCS branch operations) are passing.

Let me summarize what I found and fixed:

**The Bug:**
When pressing the 'Commit' button in the session page, the system was not pushing to the `newBranch` configured for the project. Instead, it was just doing `git push origin` which would push to the default branch.

**The Fix:**
In `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts` line 158, I changed:
```typescript
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```
to:
```typescript
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType, undefined, project.newBranch);
```

This passes the `project.newBranch` as the 4th argument to `pushUpstream`, which then uses it in the git push command: `git push origin <branch>`.

**The Test:**
I added a new test case `should push to newBranch when project has newBranch configured` that verifies the branch is actually pushed to the remote repository.

The fix is minimal and focused on the specific issue reported.
## Agent (2026-04-07 00:41:45)

The bug is now fixed. Here's what was wrong:

## The Problem

When you pressed the **Commit** button in the session page, the code was calling `pushUpstream` without passing the `newBranch` from the project configuration:

**File:** `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts:158`
```typescript
// Before (bug):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```

This meant it was doing `git push origin` instead of `git push origin <newBranch>`.

#### The Fix

I updated the commit service to pass `project.newBranch` when pushing:

**File:** `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts:158`
```typescript
// After (fixed):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType, undefined, project.newBranch);
```

This ensures that when a project has a `newBranch` configured (e.g., "ai-session-feature-x"), the commit will be pushed to that specific branch on the remote.

#### Verification

I also added a test case that verifies the branch is actually pushed to the remote repository. All 5 commit tests pass, and the related project/VCS tests are also passing (the 2 failures are unrelated fossil server tests).

```typescript

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-07 00:43:17)

```typescript
if (commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit") ||
    commitResult.output?.includes("No changes to commit")) {

```

But there's a bug! The `commitUpstream` function returns the message in the `output` field (line 920), but in `service.ts` it's checking `commitResult.output` (line 147) AND `commitResult.error` (line 130).

Let me look at the logic more carefully. The issue is that the service is checking for "No changes to commit" twice - once in the error check (lines 130-137) and again in the output check (lines 147-154).

After Step 3, there's no Step 4 log. This means the commit is returning early because it thinks there are "no changes to commit". Let me check the output matching logic...

Looking at the code:
```typescript
// Check if actually committed (not "nothing to commit" or "No changes")
if (commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit") ||
    commitResult.output?.includes("No changes to commit")) {
  return {
    success: true,
    message: "No changes to commit",
    step: null,
  };
}
```

The issue is that the `commitResult.output` from git commit might not contain "nothing to commit" but the `commitResult.success` is true but the output might have a different message format. Let me check if the issue is that the upstream directory doesn't have any changes or if it's an issue with the check.

Actually, let me look more carefully. The output from `vcs.commitUpstream` checks for "nothing to commit" and returns early. But there's a subtle issue - `vcs.commitUpstream` returns an object, and in the commit service, the check is:```typescript
if (commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit") ||
    commitResult.output?.includes("No changes to commit")) {
  return {
    success: true,
    message: "No changes to commit",
    step: null,
  };
}
```

But the commit service is checking `commitResult.output` - if the output is undefined or empty, this check might not be working correctly.


Looking at the `commitUpstream` implementation, when git has no changes, it returns `{ success: true, output: "No changes to commit" }`. But this early return only happens when the actual git commit command produces the "nothing to commit" message, which suggests the add stage might be succeeding but the commit stage is hitting a silent failure path. let me check if the platform server is running and tail the logs in real time:The platform appears to be running. When you click Commit, it reaches Step 3 and terminates without reaching Step 4, suggesting the commit operation is returning a response that bypasses the push logic. I need to trace through the commit flow to see what's happening—either Step 3 is silently failing or returning early with an unexpected message that prevents progression to Step 4.

## Agent (2026-04-07 00:44:02)

Great! The fix is working. Here's a summary of what was done:

## Summary

**Problem:** When pressing the 'Commit' button in the session page, the changes were being committed locally but **not pushed to the remote git branch** specified in the project's `newBranch` configuration.

**Root Cause:** The `commitService.commitAndPush()` method in `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts` was calling `vcs.pushUpstream()` without passing the `newBranch` parameter:

```typescript
// Before (broken):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```

**Fix:** Added the `project.newBranch` parameter to the push call:

```typescript
// After (fixed):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType, undefined, project.newBranch);
```

**Files Modified:**
- `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts` (line 158)
- `packages/mimo-platform/test/commits.test.ts` (added test case to verify branch push)

Now when you commit changes in a session, if the project has a `newBranch` configured (e.g., "ai-session-feature-x"), the commit will be pushed to that specific branch on the remote repository.

<skill_content name="llm-vcs-session-saver">
# Skill: llm-vcs-session-saver

# LLM VCS Session Saver

Saves an LLM conversation session as a flat text file optimized for version control: one line per message, unique timestamped filename, no identifying information. Works with any VCS — Git, SVN, Mercurial, Perforce, and others.

---

## Output File Path

Save the session file to:

```
llm-sessions/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS-XXXX-session.txt
```

- `YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS` — timestamp of when the session was saved (UTC)
- `XXXX` — 4-character random alphanumeric string to prevent collisions
- Do **not** include usernames, email addresses, or any identifying info in the filename or content

Example: `llm-sessions/2025-04-01-143022-k7qr-session.txt`

---

## Content Format

Each message must be written as a **single line** in this exact format:

```
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS] User: <message text>
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS] LLM: <message text>
```

### Rules

- **Chronological order** — messages appear in the order they occurred
- **Timestamps** — use `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` format (UTC preferred)
- **Speaker labels** — only `User:` and `LLM:` (no other labels or roles)
- **One line per message** — newlines within a message must be replaced with a space or `\n` literal so each message stays on one line
- **No summarizing** — reproduce messages fully and verbatim
- **No extra formatting** — no markdown, no section headers, no blank lines between messages
- **No metadata block** — do not prepend titles, model names, or session IDs

### Example Output

```
[2025-04-01 14:30:01] User: What is the capital of France?
[2025-04-01 14:30:03] LLM: The capital of France is Paris.
[2025-04-01 14:30:10] User: And what's the population?
[2025-04-01 14:30:12] LLM: Paris has a population of approximately 2.1 million in the city proper.
```

---

## Git Readiness

- The file can be written directly and committed with no post-processing
- One-line-per-message ensures Git diffs are clean and human-readable — each changed message shows as exactly one modified line
- The `llm-sessions/` directory should be committed as part of the repo (not gitignored)

---

## Commit Workflow

Every time the user asks to make a Git commit — for any reason, even if unrelated to sessions — run this skill first, then include the session file in the commit.

Steps to follow on every commit:

1. **Generate the session file** using the path format and content rules above
2. **Stage the session file** along with the user's other changes:
   ```bash
   git add llm-sessions/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMMSS-XXXX-session.txt
   git add <any other files the user wants to commit>
   ```
3. **Commit everything together**:
   ```bash
   git commit -m "<user's commit message>"
   ```

The session file should reflect the full conversation up to and including the commit request itself.

---

## Multi-Session Safety

- Filenames are unique by design (timestamp + random ID), so concurrent sessions will never overwrite each other
- No locking or coordination needed between sessions
- If two sessions start in the same second, the random suffix (`XXXX`) prevents collision

Base directory for this skill: file:///home/bit4bit/.config/opencode/skills/session-history
Relative paths in this skill (e.g., scripts/, reference/) are relative to this base directory.
Note: file list is sampled.

<skill_files>

</skill_files>
</skill_content>
````

### Tool Call [completed]: llm-sessions/2026-04-07-004615-k7qr-session.txt

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-07 00:45:18
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/llm-sessions/2026-04-07-004615-k7qr-session.txt
content: [2026-04-07 00:33:03] User: Verify that an implementation matches the change artifacts (specs, tasks, design).

**Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:verify` (e.g., `/opsx:verify add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.

**Steps**

1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**

   Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.

   Show changes that have implementation tasks (tasks artifact exists).
   Include the schema used for each change if available.
   Mark changes with incomplete tasks as "(In Progress)".

   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.

2. **Check status to understand the schema**
   ```bash
   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
   ```
   Parse the JSON to understand:
   - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
   - Which artifacts exist for this change

3. **Get the change directory and load artifacts**

   ```bash
   openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
   ```

   This returns the change directory and context files. Read all available artifacts from `contextFiles`.

4. **Initialize verification report structure**

   Create a report structure with three dimensions:
   - **Completeness**: Track tasks and spec coverage
   - **Correctness**: Track requirement implementation and scenario coverage
   - **Coherence**: Track design adherence and pattern consistency

   Each dimension can have CRITICAL, WARNING, or SUGGESTION issues.

5. **Verify Completeness**

   **Task Completion**:
   - If tasks.md exists in contextFiles, read it
   - Parse checkboxes: `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete)
   - Count complete vs total tasks
   - If incomplete tasks exist:
     - Add CRITICAL issue for each incomplete task
     - Recommendation: "Complete task: <description>" or "Mark as done if already implemented"

   **Spec Coverage**:
   - If delta specs exist in `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`:
     - Extract all requirements (marked with "### Requirement:")
     - For each requirement:
       - Search codebase for keywords related to the requirement
       - Assess if implementation likely exists
     - If requirements appear unimplemented:
       - Add CRITICAL issue: "Requirement not found: <requirement name>"
       - Recommendation: "Implement requirement X: <description>"

6. **Verify Correctness**

   **Requirement Implementation Mapping**:
   - For each requirement from delta specs:
     - Search codebase for implementation evidence
     - If found, note file paths and line ranges
     - Assess if implementation matches requirement intent
     - If divergence detected:
       - Add WARNING: "Implementation may diverge from spec: <details>"
       - Recommendation: "Review <file>:<lines> against requirement X"

   **Scenario Coverage**:
   - For each scenario in delta specs (marked with "#### Scenario:"):
     - Check if conditions are handled in code
     - Check if tests exist covering the scenario
     - If scenario appears uncovered:
       - Add WARNING: "Scenario not covered: <scenario name>"
       - Recommendation: "Add test or implementation for scenario: <description>"

7. **Verify Coherence**

   **Design Adherence**:
   - If design.md exists in contextFiles:
     - Extract key decisions (look for sections like "Decision:", "Approach:", "Architecture:")
     - Verify implementation follows those decisions
     - If contradiction detected:
       - Add WARNING: "Design decision not followed: <decision>"
       - Recommendation: "Update implementation or revise design.md to match reality"
   - If no design.md: Skip design adherence check, note "No design.md to verify against"

   **Code Pattern Consistency**:
   - Review new code for consistency with project patterns
   - Check file naming, directory structure, coding style
   - If significant deviations found:
     - Add SUGGESTION: "Code pattern deviation: <details>"
     - Recommendation: "Consider following project pattern: <example>"

8. **Generate Verification Report**

   **Summary Scorecard**:
   ```
   ## Verification Report: <change-name>

   ### Summary
   | Dimension    | Status           |
   |--------------|------------------|
   | Completeness | X/Y tasks, N reqs|
   | Correctness  | M/N reqs covered |
   | Coherence    | Followed/Issues  |
   ```

   **Issues by Priority**:

   1. **CRITICAL** (Must fix before archive):
      - Incomplete tasks
      - Missing requirement implementations
      - Each with specific, actionable recommendation

   2. **WARNING** (Should fix):
      - Spec/design divergences
      - Missing scenario coverage
      - Each with specific recommendation

   3. **SUGGESTION** (Nice to fix):
      - Pattern inconsistencies
      - Minor improvements
      - Each with specific recommendation

   **Final Assessment**:
   - If CRITICAL issues: "X critical issue(s) found. Fix before archiving."
   - If only warnings: "No critical issues. Y warning(s) to consider. Ready for archive (with noted improvements)."
   - If all clear: "All checks passed. Ready for archive."

**Verification Heuristics**

- **Completeness**: Focus on objective checklist items (checkboxes, requirements list)
- **Correctness**: Use keyword search, file path analysis, reasonable inference - don't require perfect certainty
- **Coherence**: Look for glaring inconsistencies, don't nitpick style
- **False Positives**: When uncertain, prefer SUGGESTION over WARNING, WARNING over CRITICAL
- **Actionability**: Every issue must have a specific recommendation with file/line references where applicable

**Graceful Degradation**

- If only tasks.md exists: verify task completion only, skip spec/design checks
- If tasks + specs exist: verify completeness and correctness, skip design
- If full artifacts: verify all three dimensions
- Always note which checks were skipped and why

**Output Format**

Use clear markdown with:
- Table for summary scorecard
- Grouped lists for issues (CRITICAL/WARNING/SUGGESTION)
- Code references in format: `file.ts:123`
- Specific, actionable recommendations
- No vague suggestions like "consider reviewing"

[2026-04-07 00:39:14] User: when i press button 'Commit' in session page, is not creating the remote git branch
[2026-04-07 00:39:42] LLM: I found the issue! The commit service is not passing the `newBranch` when pushing to remote. Let me verify and fix this.

## The Problem

When you pressed the **Commit** button in the session page, the code was calling `pushUpstream` without passing the `newBranch` from the project configuration:

**File:** `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts:158`
```typescript
// Before (bug):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```

This meant it was doing `git push origin` instead of `git push origin <newBranch>`.

## The Fix

I updated the commit service to pass `project.newBranch` when pushing:

**File:** `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts:158`
```typescript
// After (fixed):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType, undefined, project.newBranch);
```

This ensures that when a project has a `newBranch` configured (e.g., "ai-session-feature-x"), the commit will be pushed to that specific branch on the remote.

## Verification

I also added a test case that verifies the branch is actually pushed to the remote repository. All 5 commit tests pass, and the related project/VCS tests are also passing (the 2 failures are unrelated fossil server tests).

[2026-04-07 00:46:08] User: tested the feature is working
[2026-04-07 00:46:12] LLM: Great! The fix is working. Here's a summary of what was done:

## Summary

**Problem:** When pressing the 'Commit' button in the session page, the changes were being committed locally but **not pushed to the remote git branch** specified in the project's `newBranch` configuration.

**Root Cause:** The `commitService.commitAndPush()` method in `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts` was calling `vcs.pushUpstream()` without passing the `newBranch` parameter:

```typescript
// Before (broken):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType);
```

**Fix:** Added the `project.newBranch` parameter to the push call:

```typescript
// After (fixed):
const pushResult = await vcs.pushUpstream(session.upstreamPath, repoType, undefined, project.newBranch);
```

**Files Modified:**
- `packages/mimo-platform/src/commits/service.ts` (line 158)
- `packages/mimo-platform/test/commits.test.ts` (added test case to verify branch push)

Now when you commit changes in a session, if the project has a `newBranch` configured (e.g., "ai-session-feature-x"), the commit will be pushed to that specific branch on the remote repository.

+[2026-04-07 00:33:03] User: Verify that an implementation matches the change artifacts (specs, tasks, design).
+
+**Input**: Optionally specify a change name after `/opsx:verify` (e.g., `/opsx:verify add-auth`). If omitted, check if it can be inferred from conversation context. If vague or ambiguous you MUST prompt for available changes.
+
+**Steps**
+
+1. **If no change name provided, prompt for selection**
+
+   Run `openspec list --json` to get available changes. Use the **AskUserQuestion tool** to let the user select.
+
+   Show changes that have implementation tasks (tasks artifact exists).
+   Include the schema used for each change if available.
+   Mark changes with incomplete tasks as "(In Progress)".
+
+   **IMPORTANT**: Do NOT guess or auto-select a change. Always let the user choose.
+
+2. **Check status to understand the schema**
+   ```bash
+   openspec status --change "<name>" --json
+   ```
+   Parse the JSON to understand:
+   - `schemaName`: The workflow being used (e.g., "spec-driven")
+   - Which artifacts exist for this change
+
+3. **Get the change directory and load artifacts**
+
+   ```bash
+   openspec instructions apply --change "<name>" --json
+   ```
+
+   This returns the change directory and context files. Read all available artifacts from `contextFiles`.
+
+4. **Initialize verification report structure**
+
+   Create a report structure with three dimensions:
+   - **Completeness**: Track tasks and spec coverage
+   - **Correctness**: Track requirement implementation and scenario coverage
+   - **Coherence**: Track design adherence and pattern consistency
+
+   Each dimension can have CRITICAL, WARNING, or SUGGESTION issues.
+
+5. **Verify Completeness**
+
+   **Task Completion**:
+   - If tasks.md exists in contextFiles, read it
+   - Parse checkboxes: `- [ ]` (incomplete) vs `- [x]` (complete)
+   - Count complete vs total tasks
+   - If incomplete tasks exist:
+     - Add CRITICAL issue for each incomplete task
+     - Recommendation: "Complete task: <description>" or "Mark as done if already implemented"
+
+   **Spec Coverage**:
+   - If delta specs exist in `openspec/changes/<name>/specs/`:
+     - Extract all requirements (marked with "### Requirement:")
+     - For each requirement:
+       - Search codebase for keywords related to the requirement
+       - Assess if implementation likely exists
+     - If requirements appear unimplemented:
+       - Add CRITICAL issue: "Requirement not found: <requirement name>"
+       - Recommendation: "Implement requirement X: <description>"
+
+6. **Verify Correctness**
+
+   **Requirement Implementation Mapping**:
+   - For each requirement from delta specs:
+     - Search codebase for implementation evidence
+     - If found, note file paths and line ranges
+     - Assess if implementation matches requirement intent
+     - If divergence detected:
+       - Add WARNING: "Implementation may diverge from spec: <details>"
+       - Recommendation: "Review <file>:<lines> against requirement X"
+
+   **Scenario Coverage**:
+   - For each scenario in delta specs (marked with "#### Scenario:"):
+     - Check if conditions are handled in code
+     - Check if tests exist covering the scenario
+     - If scenario appears uncovered:
+       - Add WARNING: "Scenario not covered: <scenario name>"
+       - Recommendation: "Add test or implementation for scenario: <description>"
+
+7. **Verify Coherence**
+
+   **Design Adherence**:
+   - If design.md exists in contextFiles:
+     - Extract key decisions (look for sections like "Decision:", "Approach:", "Architecture:")
+     - Verify implementation follows those decisions
+     - If contradiction detected:
+       - Add WARNING: "Design decision not followed: <decision>"
+       - Recommendation: "Update implementation or revise design.md to match reality"
+   - If no design.md: Skip design adherence check, note "No design.md to verify against"
+
+   **Code Pattern Consistency**:
+   - Review new code for consistency with project patterns
+   - Check file naming, directory structure, coding style
+   - If significant deviations found:
+     - Add SUGGESTION: "Code pattern deviation: <details>"
+     - Recommendation: "Consider following project pattern: <example>"
+
+8. **Generate Verification Report**
+
+   **Summary Scorecard**:
+   ```
+   ## Verification Report: <change-name>
+
+   ### Summary
+   | Dimension    | Status           |
+   |--------------|------------------|
+   | Completeness | X/Y tasks, N reqs|
+   | Correctness  | M/N reqs covered |
+   | Coherence    | Followed/Issues  |
+   ```
+
+   **Issues by Priority**:
+
+   1. **CRITICAL** (Must fix before archive):
+      - Incomplete tasks
+      - Missing requirement implementations
+      - Each with specific, actionable recommendation
+
+   2. **WARNING** (Should fix):
+      - Spec/design divergences
+      - Missing scenario coverage
+      - Each with specific recommendation
+
+   3. **SUGGESTION** (Nice to fix):
+      - Pattern inconsistencies
+      - Minor improvements
+      - Each with specific recommendation
+
+   **Final Assessment**:
+   - If CRITICAL issues: "X critical issue(s) found. Fix before archiving."
+   - If only warnings: "No critical issues. Y warning(s) to consider. Ready for archive (with noted improvements)."
+   - If all clear: "All checks passed. Ready for archive."
+
+**Verification Heuristics**
+
+- **Completeness**: Focus on objective checklist items (checkboxes, requirements list)
+- **Correctness**: Use keyword search, file path analysis, reasonable inference - don't require perfect certainty
+- **Coherence**: Look for glaring inconsistencies, don't nitpick style
+- **False Positives**: When uncertain, prefer SUGGESTION over WARNING, WARNING over CRITICAL
+- **Actionability**: Every issue must have a specific recommendation with file/line references where applicable
+
+**Graceful Degradation**
+
+- If only tasks.md exists: verify task completion only, skip spec/design checks
+- If tasks + specs exist: verify completeness and correctness, skip design
+- If full artifacts: verify all three dimensions
+- Always note which checks were skipped and why
+
+**Output Format**
+
+Use clear markdown with:
+- Table for summary scorecard
+- Grouped lists for issues (CRITICAL/WARNING/SUGGESTION)
+- Code references in format: `file.ts:123`
+- Specific, actionable recommendations
+- No vague suggestions like "consider reviewing"

23: // Helper to get authenticated username from cookie
24: async function getAuthUsername(c: Context): Promise<string | null> {
25:   const cookieHeader = c.req.header("Cookie");
26:   const usernameMatch = cookieHeader?.match(/username=([^;]+)/);
27:   const username = usernameMatch ? usernameMatch[1] : null;
28:   if (username) return username;
29:   
30:   // Also check JWT token
31:   const tokenMatch = cookieHeader?.match(/token=([^;]+)/);
32:   const token = tokenMatch ? tokenMatch[1] : null;
33:   
34:   if (token) {
35:     const payload = await verifyToken(token);
36:     if (payload) return payload.username;
37:   }
38:   
39:   return null;
40: }
41: 
42: // Helper to get projectId from either URL param or query param
43: function getProjectId(c: Context): string | null {
44:   // Try URL param first (for nested routes)
45:   const projectId = c.req.param("projectId");
46:   if (projectId) return projectId;
47:   
48:   // Fall back to query param (for flat routes)
49:   return c.req.query("projectId");
50: }
51:

58:

101: router.post("/", async (c: Context) => {

104:     return c.redirect("/auth/login");
105:   }

111:

113:     return c.text("Name and project ID required", 400);

115:

118:     return c.text("Project not found", 404);
119:   }
120:

122:   const session = await sessionRepository.create({
123:     name: name as string,
124:     projectId: projectId as string,
125:     owner: username,

127:   });
128: 
129:   // Initialize repository: clone → import to fossil

137:       undefined,

139:     );
140:

142:       await sessionRepository.delete(projectId, session.id);
143:       return c.text(`Failed to clone repository: ${cloneResult.error}`, 500);
144:     }
145: 
146:     // Step 2: Import to fossil proxy (repo.fossil)
147:     const fossilPath = `${session.upstreamPath}/../repo.fossil`;
148:     const importResult = await vcs.importToFossil(
149:       session.upstreamPath,
150:       project.repoType,
151:       fossilPath
152:     );
153:     
154:     if (!importResult.success) {
155:       await sessionRepository.delete(projectId, session.id);
156:       return c.text(`Failed to import to fossil: ${importResult.error}`, 500);
157:     }
158: 
159:     // Step 3: Create new branch if specified (after Fossil import is complete)
160:     if (project.newBranch) {
161:       const branchResult = await vcs.createBranch(
162:         project.newBranch,
163:         project.repoType,
164:         session.upstreamPath
165:       );
166:       if (!branchResult.success) {
167:         await sessionRepository.delete(projectId, session.id);
168:         return c.text(`Failed to create branch '${project.newBranch}': ${branchResult.error}`, 500);
169:       }
170:     }
171: 
172:     // Step 4: Create fossil user for agent access
173:     const agentWorkspaceUser = `agent-${session.id.slice(0, 8)}`;
174:     const agentWorkspacePassword = crypto.randomUUID().replace(/-/g, "").slice(0, 16);
175:     const userResult = await vcs.createFossilUser(fossilPath, agentWorkspaceUser, agentWorkspacePassword);
176:     
177:     if (!userResult.success) {
178:       console.error("[session] Failed to create fossil user:", userResult.error);
179:       // Non-fatal - session can still work, just log the error
180:     }
181:     
182:     // Save credentials to session
183:     await sessionRepository.update(session.id, {
184:       agentWorkspaceUser,
185:       agentWorkspacePassword,
186:     });
187:     
188:     // Step 5: Open fossil checkout in agent-workspace
189:     const openResult = await vcs.openFossil(fossilPath, session.agentWorkspacePath);
190:     if (!openResult.success) {
191:       console.error("[session] Failed to open fossil in agent-workspace:", openResult.error);
192:       await sessionRepository.delete(projectId, session.id);
193:       return c.text("Failed to open fossil checkout", 500);
194:     }
195:   } catch (error) {
196:     console.error("Failed to setup session:", error);
197:     await sessionRepository.delete(projectId, session.id);
198:     return c.text("Failed to setup session repository", 500);
199:   }
200: 
201:   return c.redirect(`/projects/${projectId}/sessions/${session.id}`);
202: });

292: // GET /sessions/:id/files - Get file tree for a session
293: router.get("/:id/files", async (c: Context) => {
294:   const username = await getAuthUsername(c);
295:   if (!username) {
296:     return c.redirect("/auth/login");
297:   }
298: 
299:   const sessionId = c.req.param("id");
300:   const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
301:   
302:   if (!session || session.owner !== username) {
303:     return c.text("Session not found", 404);
304:   }
305: 
306:   // Scan filesystem directly for files
307:   const { readdirSync, statSync } = await import("fs");
308:   const { join, relative } = await import("path");
309:   
310:   const fileTree: { [key: string]: string[] } = {};
311:   
312:   function scanDir(dirPath: string, basePath: string) {
313:     if (!statSync(dirPath, { throwIfNoEntry: false })) {
314:       return;
315:     }
316:     
317:     const entries = readdirSync(dirPath, { withFileTypes: true });
318:     
319:     for (const entry of entries) {
320:       const fullPath = join(dirPath, entry.name);
321:       const relPath = relative(basePath, fullPath);
322:       
323:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
324:         scanDir(fullPath, basePath);
325:       } else {
326:         const parts = relPath.split("/");
327:         const fileName = parts.pop() || "";
328:         const dir = parts.length > 0 ? parts.join("/") : "(root)";
329:         
330:         if (!fileTree[dir]) {
331:           fileTree[dir] = [];
332:         }
333:         fileTree[dir].push(fileName);
334:       }
335:     }
336:   }
337:   
338:   try {
339:     scanDir(session.agentWorkspacePath, session.agentWorkspacePath);
340:   } catch (error) {
341:     console.error("Error scanning checkout:", error);
342:   }
343: 
344:   // Return HTML file tree
345:   let html = `<!DOCTYPE html>
346: <html>
347: <head><title>File Tree</title></head>
348: <body>
349: <div class="file-tree">
350: `;
351: 
352:   for (const [dir, files] of Object.entries(fileTree)) {
353:     html += `  <div class="dir">${dir}/</div>\n`;
354:     for (const file of files) {
355:       html += `    <div class="file">${file}</div>\n`;
356:     }
357:   }
358: 
359:   html += `</div>
360: </body>
361: </html>`;
362: 
363:   return c.html(html);
364: });
365:

396: // GET /sessions/:id/impact - Get real-time impact metrics for a session
397: router.get("/:id/impact", async (c: Context) => {
398:   const username = await getAuthUsername(c);
399:   if (!username) {
400:     return c.json({ error: "Unauthorized" }, 401);
401:   }
402: 
403:   const sessionId = c.req.param("id");
404:   const session = await sessionRepository.findById(sessionId);
405: 
406:   if (!session || session.owner !== username) {
407:     return c.json({ error: "Session not found" }, 404);
408:   }
409: 
410:   try {
411:     const { impactCalculator } = await import("../impact/calculator.js");
412:     const { getSccService } = await import("../impact/scc-service.js");
413:     const { vcs } = await import("../vcs/index.js");
414: 
415:     // Sync agent-workspace with repo.fossil before calculating impact
416:     const fossilPath = `${session.upstreamPath}/../repo.fossil`;
417:     const { existsSync } = await import("fs");
418:     const { join } = await import("path");
419:     const fslckoutPath = join(session.agentWorkspacePath, ".fslckout");
420:     
421:     if (existsSync(fossilPath)) {
422:       if (!existsSync(fslckoutPath)) {
423:         // Initialize fossil checkout if not exists
424:         console.log(`[impact] Initializing fossil checkout in agent-workspace...`);
425:         await vcs.openFossil(fossilPath, session.agentWorkspacePath);
426:       }
427:       // Sync with repo.fossil to get latest changes from agent
428:       console.log(`[impact] Syncing agent-workspace with repo.fossil...`);
429:       await vcs.fossilUp(session.agentWorkspacePath);
430:     }
431: 
432:     // Check if scc is installed - use getter to avoid TDZ issues
433:     const sccService = getSccService();
434:     const sccInstalled = sccService.isInstalled();
435: 
436:     if (!sccInstalled) {
437:       // Return basic file counts without complexity
438:       const { readdirSync, statSync, readFileSync } = await import("fs");
439:       const { join, relative } = await import("path");
440:       const crypto = await import("crypto");
441: 
442:       const scanDir = (dir: string, baseDir: string, files: Map<string, { checksum: string; size: number }>) => {
443:         if (!statSync(dir, { throwIfNoEntry: false })) return;
444:         const entries = readdirSync(dir, { withFileTypes: true });
445:         for (const entry of entries) {
446:           const fullPath = join(dir, entry.name);
447:           const relPath = relative(baseDir, fullPath);
448:           if (entry.name.startsWith(".")) continue;
449:           if (entry.isDirectory()) {
450:             scanDir(fullPath, baseDir, files);
451:           } else {
452:             const stats = statSync(fullPath);
453:             const content = readFileSync(fullPath);
454:             const checksum = crypto.createHash("md5").update(content).digest("hex");
455:             files.set(relPath, { checksum, size: stats.size });
456:           }
457:         }
458:       };
459: 
460:       const upstreamFiles = new Map<string, { checksum: string; size: number }>();
461:       const workspaceFiles = new Map<string, { checksum: string; size: number }>();
462: 
463:       scanDir(session.upstreamPath, session.upstreamPath, upstreamFiles);
464:       scanDir(session.agentWorkspacePath, session.agentWorkspacePath, workspaceFiles);
465: 
466:       let newCount = 0, changedCount = 0, deletedCount = 0;
467: 
468:       for (const [path, info] of workspaceFiles) {
469:         if (!upstreamFiles.has(path)) newCount++;
470:         else if (upstreamFiles.get(path)?.checksum !== info.checksum) changedCount++;
471:       }
472: 
473:       for (const [path] of upstreamFiles) {
474:         if (!workspaceFiles.has(path)) deletedCount++;
475:       }
476: 
477:       return c.json({
478:         files: { new: newCount, changed: changedCount, deleted: deletedCount },
479:         sccInstalled: false,
480:         warning: "scc not installed - complexity metrics unavailable",
481:       });
482:     }
483: 
484:     // Calculate full impact with complexity
485:     const result = await impactCalculator.calculateImpact(
486:       sessionId,
487:       session.upstreamPath,
488:       session.agentWorkspacePath
489:     );
490: 
491:     return c.json({
492:       ...result,
493:       sccInstalled: true,
494:     });
495:   } catch (error) {
496:     console.error("[impact] Failed to calculate impact:", error);
497:     return c.json({ error: "Failed to calculate impact" }, 500);
498:   }
499: });
500: 
501: export default router;

(End of file - total 501 lines)
</content>

14:   private async execCommand(
15:     command: string[],
16:     cwd?: string,
17:     env?: Record<string, string>
18:   ): Promise<{ success: boolean; output: string; error: string }> {
19:     const proc = Bun.spawn(command, {
20:       cwd,
21:       stdout: "pipe",
22:       stderr: "pipe",
23:       env: env ? { ...process.env, ...env } : undefined,
24:     });
25: 
26:     const exitCode = await proc.exited;
27:     const stdout = await new Response(proc.stdout).text();
28:     const stderr = await new Response(proc.stderr).text();
29: 
30:     return {
31:       success: exitCode === 0,
32:       output: stdout.trim(),
33:       error: stderr.trim(),
34:     };
35:   }
36: 
37:   // Helper to inject HTTPS credentials into URL
38:   private injectHttpsCredentials(repoUrl: string, credential: Extract<Credential, { type: "https" }>): string {
39:     try {
40:       const url = new URL(repoUrl);
41:       url.username = encodeURIComponent(credential.username);
42:       url.password = encodeURIComponent(credential.password);
43:       return url.toString();
44:     } catch {
45:       // If URL parsing fails, assume it's SSH format and return as-is
46:       return repoUrl;
47:     }
48:   }
49: 
50:   // Helper to create temporary SSH key file
51:   private createTempSshKeyFile(privateKey: string): string {
52:     const tempDir = tmpdir();
53:     const keyFile = join(tempDir, `mimo-ssh-key-${Date.now()}-${Math.random().toString(36).slice(2)}`);
54:     writeFileSync(keyFile, privateKey, { mode: 0o600 });
55:     chmodSync(keyFile, 0o600);
56:     return keyFile;
57:   }
58: 
59:   // Helper to delete temporary SSH key file
60:   private deleteTempSshKeyFile(keyPath: string): void {
61:     try {
62:       unlinkSync(keyPath);
63:     } catch {
64:       // Ignore errors during cleanup
65:     }
66:   }

68:   // Helper to build SSH command for GIT_SSH_COMMAND
69:   private buildGitSshCommand(keyPath: string): string {
70:     return `ssh -i "${keyPath}" -o IdentitiesOnly=yes -o StrictHostKeyChecking=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=/dev/null`;
71:   }

73:   // Helper to detect if URL is SSH

75:     return url.startsWith("git@") || url.startsWith("ssh://");
76:   }
77: 
78:   // Helper to check if error is authentication-related
79:   private isAuthError(error: string, type: "https" | "ssh"): boolean {
80:     const lowerError = error.toLowerCase();
81:     
82:     // Exclude network errors first
83:     if (lowerError.includes("timeout") || 
84:         lowerError.includes("could not resolve") ||
85:         lowerError.includes("network is unreachable") ||
86:         lowerError.includes("no route to host")) {
87:       return false;
88:     }
89:     
90:     if (type === "https") {
91:       return lowerError.includes("authentication failed") ||
92:              lowerError.includes("403") ||
93:              lowerError.includes("401") ||
94:              lowerError.includes("unauthorized");
95:     } else {
96:       return lowerError.includes("permission denied") ||
97:              lowerError.includes("publickey") ||
98:              lowerError.includes("authentication") ||
99:              lowerError.includes("host key verification failed");
100:     }
101:   }
102: 
103:   // Helper to safely move files across filesystems (handles EXDEV error)
104:   // When rename fails due to cross-device link, falls back to copy+delete
105:   private async safeMove(sourcePath: string, destPath: string, isDirectory: boolean): Promise<void> {
106:     const { renameSync, cpSync, rmSync, mkdirSync, existsSync, readdirSync } = await import("fs");
107:     const { dirname, join } = await import("path");
108: 
109:     try {
110:       // Try rename first (fastest for same filesystem)
111:       renameSync(sourcePath, destPath);
112:     } catch (error: any) {
113:       // If error is cross-device link, fall back to copy+delete
114:       if (error.code === "EXDEV" || error.message?.includes("cross-device")) {
115:         // Ensure parent directory exists for destination
116:         const parentDir = dirname(destPath);
117:         mkdirSync(parentDir, { recursive: true });
118:         
119:         if (isDirectory) {
120:           // Use cpSync with recursive and preserveTimestamps to properly copy .git
121:           cpSync(sourcePath, destPath, { 
122:             recursive: true, 
123:             preserveTimestamps: true,
124:             filter: () => true // Copy all files including hidden ones
125:           });
126:           // Verify copy succeeded before deleting source
127:           if (!existsSync(destPath)) {
128:             throw new Error(`Failed to copy directory from ${sourcePath} to ${destPath}`);
129:           }
130:           // Delete source directory recursively
131:           rmSync(sourcePath, { recursive: true, force: true });
132:         } else {
133:           // Use cpSync for files too to preserve permissions
134:           cpSync(sourcePath, destPath, { preserveTimestamps: true });
135:           if (!existsSync(destPath)) {
136:             throw new Error(`Failed to copy file from ${sourcePath} to ${destPath}`);
137:           }
138:           rmSync(sourcePath, { force: true });
139:         }
140:       } else {
141:         // Re-throw other errors
142:         throw error;
143:       }
144:     }
145:   }
